  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

        scope : 'name email',

<span id="freeTextContainer13359904560720213802">Ciri staje przed swoim przeznaczeniem. Drakkar wiozący Yennefer trafia w oko czarodziejskiego cyklonu.   <span id="freeText13359904560720213802" style="display:none">Ciri staje przed swoim przeznaczeniem. Drakkar wiozący Yennefer trafia w oko czarodziejskiego cyklonu. Czy wśród przyjaciół wiedźmina ukrywa się zdrajca? Czwarta, przedostatnia odłona epopei o świecie wiedźmina i wojnach, jakie nim wstrząsają. W zagubionej wśród bagien chacie pustelnika ciężko ranna Ciri powraca do zdrowia. Jej tropem podążają bezlitośni zabójcy z Nilfgaardu. Tymczasem drużyna Geralta, unikając coraz to nowych niebezpieczeństw, dociera wreszcie do ukrywjących się druidów. Czy wiedźminowi uda się odnaleźć Ciri? Jaką rolę odegra osnuta legendą Wieża Jaskółki?</span>
  <a data-text-id="13359904560720213802" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Not really. The Tower of the Swallow is sixth book in the Witcher series (fourth book about Geralt and Ciri), so you are not going to understand the p<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Not really. The Tower of the Swallow is sixth book in the Witcher series (fourth book about Geralt and Ciri), so you are not going to understand the plot, world, politics or characters. You really need to read the previous books to enjoy this one.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_1789889756" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1789889756" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1789889756?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780316273763" href="/book/show/30079689-the-tower-of-swallows">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1789889756" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7908776530016682069">How can I give an outline of the plot of the sixth book of a series without giving huge spoilers? So here you are, a huge spoiler:<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480207674i/21284506._SX540_.jpg' width='460' height='280' alt='Spoiler' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Sufficient to say, the book picks up right where the previous left which is logical considering that nothing whatsoever was resolved by the end of that one - actually I had a feeling it ended practically in mid-sentence. Let me just say that we will see the fate of all interesting major people from the previous installment. None of them ended up with happily ever afte</span>
  <span id="freeText7908776530016682069" style="display:none">How can I give an outline of the plot of the sixth book of a series without giving huge spoilers? So here you are, a huge spoiler:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480207674i/21284506._SX540_.jpg" width="460" height="280" alt="Spoiler" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sufficient to say, the book picks up right where the previous left which is logical considering that nothing whatsoever was resolved by the end of that one - actually I had a feeling it ended practically in mid-sentence. Let me just say that we will see the fate of all interesting major people from the previous installment. None of them ended up with happily ever after situation. Some got killed, including the people that really deserved it. <br><br>One point of notice: we got to have Dandelion's (Jaskier in some translations) POV in form of his memoirs - he started compiling them for the lack of nothing else to do to break the monotony. In case anybody had any doubt about the guy being one of the most colorful character of the series: after reading this part your doubts will go away never to return again. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480208569i/21284581.jpg" width="290" height="435" alt="Dandelion" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Unfortunately the passage in question is not very long, but for me it was the best part of the book bar none.<br><br>Something else to note: in terms of violence the novel has more of it than all the previous combined. People get killed, maimed, tortured, etc. This combined with the fact that the second half slowed down from very fast action of the first part forced me to lower the rating by one; I really liked the beginning. <br><br>Readers that made it this far know that Sapkowski loves jumping back and force in time while spinning his tale. Let me assure you: you ain't seen nothing yet until you read this novel. These jumps made my head spin giving me a complete illusion of riding a giant roller-coaster. I have to give it to the author: he does it without creating any lasting confusion. I do not recall this particular trick used to such effect anywhere. <br><br>In the end I have to say that if managed to finish this next-to-last book of a series, it is too late to give up now. On to the last book we go! </span>
  <a data-text-id="7908776530016682069" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1953781294" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1953781294" />
    <a title="Joey Woolfardis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4639825-joey-woolfardis"><img alt="Joey Woolfardis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490696206p2/4639825.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1953781294?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joey Woolfardis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joey Woolfardis" href="/user/show/4639825-joey-woolfardis">Joey Woolfardis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781473211568" href="/book/show/18247597-the-tower-of-the-swallow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=ce20">ce20</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=bloody-cack">bloody-cack</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=polish">polish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=masculine">masculine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=bookshelf">bookshelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=myths-magic-and-mordor">myths-magic-and-mordor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4639825-joey-woolfardis?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1953781294" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18367786751142331771"><i>This review can be found on <a href='http://amaranthinereads.blogspot.co.uk/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amaranthine Reads</a></i>.<br/><br/>The <i>Witcher</i> series by Polish author Andrzej Sapkowski continues, with the Child Surprise Ciri travelling around with a bunch of thieves and bandits called the Rats, whilst Geralt, sorcerers and the Emperor send out people to find her.<br/><br/>This series has plummeted to the very depths of tedium. Every book has melded in to one and it's difficult for me to remember this particular one, though I do recall my consternation at the random change of narrative sty</span>
  <span id="freeText18367786751142331771" style="display:none"><i>This review can be found on <a href="http://amaranthinereads.blogspot.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Amaranthine Reads</a></i>.<br /><br />The <i>Witcher</i> series by Polish author Andrzej Sapkowski continues, with the Child Surprise Ciri travelling around with a bunch of thieves and bandits called the Rats, whilst Geralt, sorcerers and the Emperor send out people to find her.<br /><br />This series has plummeted to the very depths of tedium. Every book has melded in to one and it's difficult for me to remember this particular one, though I do recall my consternation at the random change of narrative style. Geralt is still not doing any Witchering, there is still monumental bitching between all the female characters and the dialogue is still pitiful.<br /><br />I complained during a review of an earlier book in this series that we rarely had other points of view during the narration, which seemed to slow down the entire thing. This book rectifies that, but in such a way that it may as well have not happened. We have around five POVs during any given chapter, which confuses things incredibly and don't actually improve the plot or pace of the action. We also, for some reason, begin to get excerpts from Dandelion's little memoirs, which add nothing to the plot except a general feel that perhaps this is something Sapkowski should maybe try out because it's cool, yo.<br /><br />The plot is also the same as it was in the previous three books. This series, a five book series discounting the first two short story collections, is definitely two books too long and probably four books too long. Everything seems to take around two chapters to tell. A journey that could be told in one sentence ends up taking approximately half the book and we are left wondering why. Nothing particularly exciting happens during these journeys, except meeting new characters that add nothing to the story because the characters we already know are weak and two dimensional. Their interaction is always so false and incredibly immature.<br /><br />Speaking of the characters, the protagonists known as Geralt and Ciri have become cantankerous and pathetic. They whinge and moan and act like little children not getting their own way. And yet no-one minds because one is a part of a prophecy and the other characters are all in love with the other. It is as if nothing can touch them-which is apparently the case since they elude capture, maiming and death numerous times through no reason other than they must to keep the story going.<br /><br />There is also far, far, far too many mentions of genitals. I have never read a book that is so obsessed with genitals and sex. I'm sure HBO would love to turn this in to a TV series-and a successful one at that-due to the sheer amount of tits and sex. Someone is either aiming to stab someone else in the penis or a man is wanting to shove his penis in a woman's vagina. This is basically all that happens, with some killing in between.<br /><br />And there is still endless bitching between the female characters. I'm not sure there is a single woman who have anything nice to say about another woman, except Ciri but she's basically just a child anyway. And all women <i>
  <b>love</b>
</i> all children. It's a fact.<br /><br />I don't know why I felt the need to finish this series. There is one book to go after this and whilst I found this particular instalment as boring as any book can be, I find I've invested so much I need to know. Belzebub knows I will be disappointed: I can feel it with this book as the plot meanders, the characters flatten out even more and the dialogue improves by a hair's breadth. It is my own fault for wasting my own time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18367786751142331771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2600917153" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2600917153" />
    <a title="James Tivendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10282461-james-tivendale"><img alt="James Tivendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605206526p2/10282461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2600917153?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Tivendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Tivendale" href="/user/show/10282461-james-tivendale">James Tivendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781473211568" href="/book/show/18247597-the-tower-of-the-swallow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10282461-james-tivendale?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2600917153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11234000423185445269">I received a review copy of The Tower of the Swallow in exchange for an honest review. Thank you to Andrzej Sapkowski and Gollancz. Minor spoilers may follow. <br/><br/>The narrative begins with a hermit called Vysogota finding what he believes is an injured boy in a forest. It transpires that this young gentleman is actually the girl, Ciri and she is very close to death. The hermit takes her to his shack which is untraceable unless you know it's there and prays that he can aid her recovery. He was formal</span>
  <span id="freeText11234000423185445269" style="display:none">I received a review copy of The Tower of the Swallow in exchange for an honest review. Thank you to Andrzej Sapkowski and Gollancz. Minor spoilers may follow. <br /><br />The narrative begins with a hermit called Vysogota finding what he believes is an injured boy in a forest. It transpires that this young gentleman is actually the girl, Ciri and she is very close to death. The hermit takes her to his shack which is untraceable unless you know it's there and prays that he can aid her recovery. He was formally a scholar and a medical practitioner which is fortunate. <br /><br />"He involuntarily drew back and hissed at the site of the ghastly mask of dirt and congealed blood where the boy's face should have been."<br /><br />After days of assistance, constantly watching and caring, Ciri slowly recovers. She wishes to leave straight away, to escape, as it transpires that a bounty hunter called Bonhart is tracking her. The former scholar guarantees that there is no possibility that they can be found and to heal first before venturing out. The duo get to know each other and exchange stories. Firstly, the Hermit explains who he is and why he lives in such isolation. Following that, Ciri - The Child of Destiny - explains what has happened to her since the ending of Baptism of Fire and this is where the story really starts. This is the main storyline for forty percent of the novel but is not all included at the beginning and after certain segments, they will conclude the story and reflect, and do chores. <br /><br />"Had someone crept up after nightfall to the cottage with the sunken, moss-grown thatched roof, had they peered inside, in the dimly lit interior they would have seen a grey-bearded old man listening to a tale told by an ashen-haired girl sitting on a log by the fireplace."<br /><br />Another frequent storyline that is presented is regarding Geralt and his band of companions including a vampire, an archer, a poet and a traitor swordsman as they aim to trace the druids who may know about Ciri's true whereabouts. These sections were brilliant. It's not just these two train of events that we follow, however. There is a large amount of point of view perspectives and occasionally after getting my teeth firmly set into a stunning set-piece or chuckling at some rollickingly good banter, Sapkowski would then throw us somewhere else in this extravagantly large and detailed world to follow individuals who I wasn't at all familiar with. Initially, it was a buzzkill - but in these segments, after two-pages of missing Geralt or Ciri, it actually seemed to make sense why this was presented in this manner, and I can conclude when the finale approaches - you will, or at least I was, very impressed with the overall structure. Although certain times the choice of the next point of view chapter did seem sporadic and slightly random.<br /><br />I've mentioned previously that in this series I find the characters to be exquisite. Much has happened to the main two characters - Geralt and Ciri. They have developed spectacularly across these six novels and in a way have almost swapped places. I won't explain that statement as might approach spoiler territory but see if you agree after you've finished this narrative. Also, if you are thinking of approaching this series just because you enjoyed the Witcher games, since The Sword of Destiny, it is very rare that Geralt has actually just gone solo monster-hunting. If anything, as the saga progresses it's almost presenting the real monsters as being the politics, corruption, warring nations and all people involved. Geralt, who never ever questioned good or evil as long as he was paid for what he was doing is brooding a lot but also changing his outlook on the world. His number one objective is to find Ciri and will do all in his power to do that. <br /><br />One of my qualms about previous entries was about needless information dumping sections about political happenings one hundred years ago or who married someone else previously and what effect it had on characters I don't know. They distracted from the main story and thus far haven't heightened my enjoyment at all. There is only one such section here and although I did want to skip past it, it was an okay read but still seemed a bit like a dull interlude. <br /><br />All in all, this was an extraordinary tale which highlights Sapkowski's masterful character creation - many of who will stay in my mind long after I complete this saga - and often astonishingly exciting set pieces. Especially the scene including ice-skates! The storytelling is also top-notch barring the occasional hiccup I've mentioned in my reviews thus far. Only one book remains for me now - excluding Season of Storms which is set prior to the main set of novels - and I'm intrigued to see how this can all be wrapped up in just one book. It seems like a phenomenal ask but I'm going to jump in straight away and see if Sapkowski can fulfill the promise he has flaunted thus far of being able to make this one of the best fantasy sagas of all time. Conclusions are very important to me so I'll let you know if I believe he succeeds in my next review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11234000423185445269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2012352295" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2012352295" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8836060-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487160141p2/8836060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2012352295?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/8836060-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35062472-the-tower-of-swallows">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8836060-michelle?shelf=witcherverse">witcherverse</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2012352295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2633900311979563148">I really really want to love this book, but the honest truth is that --this one is really not that great. “The Tower of Swallows is a difficult book to define, or even to recap. The writing feels lost: ambling around without direction, constantly jumping scenes, and forgetting about Geralt altogether about half-way through the book. <br/><br/>Of note, “The Tower of Swallows” isn't really about the eponymous witcher, Geralt of Rivia. Most real estate is devoted to Ciri telling the story of how she escaped </span>
  <span id="freeText2633900311979563148" style="display:none">I really really want to love this book, but the honest truth is that --this one is really not that great. “The Tower of Swallows is a difficult book to define, or even to recap. The writing feels lost: ambling around without direction, constantly jumping scenes, and forgetting about Geralt altogether about half-way through the book. <br /><br />Of note, “The Tower of Swallows” isn't really about the eponymous witcher, Geralt of Rivia. Most real estate is devoted to Ciri telling the story of how she escaped Bonhart, a deeply menacing bounty hunter of unclear motivations; his erstwhile employer, Nilfgaardian coroner Stefan Skellen; and the Archmage Vilgefortz, who appears to be the series' main antagonist. Eventually she leaves her hiding place to make her way to the tower, followed by said pursuers, who are determined to catch her before she can enter the tower and reassume her powers. Geralt and his companions, meanwhile, are trying to make their way to Ciri or to where they believe she might be. Yennefer and Triss are also on Ciri's path, albeit on different timelines, and likely for different reasons. <br /><br />The character narratives are not always linear, or even told straightforwardly in the close third person favored by the genre. Yennefer's story, for example, is told over several timelines, with crucial parts related by individuals who may not be reliable narrators. More often than not, the stylistic gambit works, but there are instances in which “The Tower of Swallows” would have benefitted from more conventional plotting. For example, there is far too much space given to the spy Dijkstra's visit to a far-flung (and newly introduced) kingdom--a plot point that doesn't really develop and, frankly, isn't necessary. Sometimes the same event is narrated by different narrators from different times. Then there's this build up that always starts with the same words and goes nowhere: "if someone looked into the cottage, they would have seen an ashen haired girl…” It says it like 7 times, and it's a full paragraph of text. Every time I read it, it heightens my anticipation for bigger things to come -- but nothing ever happens! It feels like Andrzej Sapkowski got bored, and just decided to jump around and experiment with the story from different angles --then decided to throw the whole mess together and call it a book. <br /><br />It's also worth noting the gratuitous violence --the most I have encountered in series so far. Without spoiling too much, there's a great deal of focus on torture and humiliation during certain sequences, and though it has its purpose -- was uncomfortable to read.<br /><br />Just as it gets interesting, it abruptly ends. There's little resolution, and half the characters are lost in limbo. Who knows where the hell Geralt is?! I get that it's trying to set up the next book, but the ending scene is strangely flat. There's little to suggest doom or hope --it just ends. This is, by far, the weakest book in the series. “Time of Contempt” was another tier of quality. I still think this is a superb series, and I hope “Lady of The Lake” will be a worthy finale.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2633900311979563148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2127438607" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2127438607" />
    <a title="Sr3yas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23097409-sr3yas"><img alt="Sr3yas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520526764p2/23097409.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2127438607?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sr3yas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sr3yas" href="/user/show/23097409-sr3yas">Sr3yas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/29340636-the-tower-of-swallows">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2127438607" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17345915967484190374"><b>Believe it or not, the hero of this installment is not the Witcher, Yennefer or Ciri.</b> It's Andrzej Sapkowski and his masterful storytelling technique, which utilizes various POVs, narrative styles and multiple timelines across the centuries and locations. He weaves a narrative yarn which should have been confusing but surprisingly turns out to be fresh, sharp and fun to read.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1511090035i/24481630.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I bow down before you in supreme awe.<br/><br/><i>Mild spoilers are the necessary evil, they are necessary.</i><br/> ----------------- Sreyas, t</span>
  <span id="freeText17345915967484190374" style="display:none"><b>Believe it or not, the hero of this installment is not the Witcher, Yennefer or Ciri.</b> It's Andrzej Sapkowski and his masterful storytelling technique, which utilizes various POVs, narrative styles and multiple timelines across the centuries and locations. He weaves a narrative yarn which should have been confusing but surprisingly turns out to be fresh, sharp and fun to read.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1511090035i/24481630.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I bow down before you in supreme awe.<br><br><i>Mild spoilers are the necessary evil, they are necessary.</i><br> ----------------- Sreyas, the tales of <u>
  <b>SPOILERS AHEAD</b>
</u><br><br>The last installment had very little narrative space for Ciri and Yennefer <i>(no complaints there)</i>, but this one brutally revamps Ciri as on hell of a character by pushing her limits like never before. At the risk of sounding corny, let me say Ciri is like a diamond, and in Tower of Swallows, they cut her. <br><br>The story opens with Ciri, who recounts her tale to a Hermit named Vysogota, who found her wounded in his forest. Sapkowski did an excellent job with these two characters and their interactions, effectively building CIri's story arc with the old school storytelling method.<br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1511090035i/24481634._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>*Ciri and Vysogoto chilling*</i><br><br><b>Witcher's story arc is still my personal favorite</b> because of the company he keeps and the adventures he stumbles on to. In this installment, Witcher's fellowship adds a new young member to their ranks and this completes the <i>adopted dysfunctional family of Witcher.</i> The scene where Geralt accuse Cahir of betrayal and the mayhem that follows afterward was spectacularly hilarious, proving once again the colorfulness of Geralt and his company. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1511090035i/24481632._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yennefer once again gets least screen time, and once again her chapter blew me away with complex narrative style and sheer visual spectacle. I was never a fan of Yennefer before this book, but now I am a fan. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1511090035i/24481633._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>What makes this volume stand out from others</b> is the bold narration and widened explanation of what the hell has been going on outside the main characters. All the installment before Swallows gave me an impression that I am looking at the great Nifflegardian War through the wrong end of the telescope. Tower of Swallow finally confronts or at least untangles the politics of war and character motivations through chapters featuring Twany owl as well as Dijkstra. <br><br>I especially loved Dijkstra's chapter, the last pages of this chapter was storytelling at its best.<br><br>Swallows even stepped up the action. The action scenes featuring Witcher and Co were complete mayhem as always, and there are many memorable moments.But Ciri stole the show with amazing finale fight on the ice. Seriously, words fail me!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1511090035i/24481629._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And appropriately, the artist featured the battle on Ice near Tower of Swallows Spanish edition cover. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1511090035i/24481631.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Needless to say, My love for Spanish edition covers continue.<br><br>I want to talk more about stuff like how assassin Bonhart reminds me of DC's Deathstroke, and I want to talk about how fascinated I am with world of Witcher because of some crazy and similar aspects it share with our own world (Months, twisted Norse mythology, festivals), and Spawaski's writing style which at one point reminded me of old western. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(Rat's last stand) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>But I don't think there will be enough space and moreover, I don't think I can put them in words properly!<br><br><b>So TL: DR? Another great installment in Witcher series!</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1511090035i/24481635._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_3211556194" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3211556194" />
    <a title="Deborah Obida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida"><img alt="Deborah Obida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604679377p2/54790180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3211556194?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Obida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Obida" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida">Deborah Obida</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/29340636-the-tower-of-swallows">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3211556194" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12321260650863881468">Tower of Swallows is another great instalment to the Witcher series. Though I love it and think it's a great book I have a few issues with this.<br/>●I didn't like the way the story is told<br/>●Geralt was barely in this, the part that he was in was almost inconsequential.<br/>●The writing is below average, I think it has something to do with the translation.<br/><br/>Apart from the above I pretty much like everything about this book. Just how <i>Baptism of Fire</i> was Geralt's book this is Ciri's book. The plot follows Ciri'</span>
  <span id="freeText12321260650863881468" style="display:none">Tower of Swallows is another great instalment to the Witcher series. Though I love it and think it's a great book I have a few issues with this.<br />●I didn't like the way the story is told<br />●Geralt was barely in this, the part that he was in was almost inconsequential.<br />●The writing is below average, I think it has something to do with the translation.<br /><br />Apart from the above I pretty much like everything about this book. Just how <i>Baptism of Fire</i> was Geralt's book this is Ciri's book. The plot follows Ciri's life after the Rats were killed. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>It isn’t the evil and indecent who are flung down into the depths, no! Oh, no! The evil and decisive fling down those who are moral, honest and noble but maladroit, hesitant and full of scruples.</i>
</b><br /><br />Ciri was baldly injured and was found by Vysogota an old hermit who treated her. While she was there healing she told him her story. We finally got to know how she got injured and how Bonhart captured her. Ciri is still smart but life has changed her, she is now somewhat bitter and very vengeful. Living with Vysogota for some months really helped her. I'm also glad she now knows that her love ones didn't abandon her.<br /><br />Dandelion's narrative was a breathe of fresh air, I had fun reading that. Too bad it was short. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>Swimming, to put it mildly, was–and is–not one of my strong points. Had Mother Nature wanted me to swim, in the act of creation and the process of evolution she would have equipped me with webbed fingers.</i>
</b><br /><br />Geralt made some few discoveries about the prophesy about Ciri. He finally found the Druids he was looking for but he got distracted, I know that is the author's way of dragging the story, but by doing that he is ruining his character.<br /><br />Yennefer is also here, her search for Ciri is even more effective than Geralt's half baked plan. I love her strength, loyalty and dedication. I never knew she cared this much for Ciri.<br /><br />Cahir, Milva, Regis and the rest of the gang are still here, they even have a new addition, her name is Angoulême, she is from Cintra.<br /><br />This ended in a cliffhanger, only Geralt was safe, Ciri and Yennefer are both in a peril.<br /><br />This conversation really got me thinking, it's insulting but true.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>‘Do you know, Witcher, what the greatest snag of longevity is?’<br />‘No.’<br />‘Sex.’<br />‘What?’<br />‘You heard right. Sex. After almost a hundred years it becomes boring. There’s nothing in it to fascinate or excite any longer, nothing that has the exciting appeal of novelty. It has all been done already… In this or that way, but it has happened. And then suddenly comes the Conjunction of the Spheres and you, people, appear here. Human survivors, come from another world, from your former world, which you managed utterly to destroy with your still-hirsute hands, barely five million years after evolving as a species. There’s only a handful of you, your life expectancy is ridiculously low, so your survival depends on the pace of reproduction. Thus unbridled lust never leaves you, sex totally governs you; it’s a drive more powerful even than the survival instinct. To die? Why not, if one can fuck around beforehand. That is your entire philosophy.’</i>
</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12321260650863881468" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer5575063832638690567">This is a story about family, friendship, love and loyalty. It’s funny, heartwarming and sarcastic, It’s brutal, unforgiving, and disturbing. It’s also relentless in the way it keeps expanding the infinite grayscale that drives the actions and choices of the characters; with believable character interactions. You need to be one hundred percent focused to keep-up with the twist, turns, and time jumps, if you’re able to keep that focus, the story told is absolutely fantastic. <br/>I really like the wri</span>
  <span id="freeText5575063832638690567" style="display:none">This is a story about family, friendship, love and loyalty. It’s funny, heartwarming and sarcastic, It’s brutal, unforgiving, and disturbing. It’s also relentless in the way it keeps expanding the infinite grayscale that drives the actions and choices of the characters; with believable character interactions. You need to be one hundred percent focused to keep-up with the twist, turns, and time jumps, if you’re able to keep that focus, the story told is absolutely fantastic. <br />I really like the writing style of the author. The story and the characters are extremely captivating. I am impressed by how Sapkowski creatively plays with different narrative techniques. The Witcher’s storyline is told in a series of diary entries written by Dandelion, most of Ciri’s part of the story is told as a series of courtroom testimonies and flashbacks.<br /><br />A new character, Leo Bonhart, the vicious bounty hunter, has some terrifying scene, as is the gladiator scene set in a coliseum. At the end of the book there’s a spectacular battle in which Ciri is on ice skates.<br /></span>

<div id="review_3017120152" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3017120152" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1170391-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590218363p2/1170391.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3017120152?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/1170391-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/51194509-the-tower-of-the-swallow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=translated">translated</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3017120152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4949287189111411159">I'm currently self isolating with covid 19 symptoms and this was everything I needed right now.<br/><br/>As I always say in these Witcher reviews - these books are not going to be for everyone. There's a lot of, often dry, political and court talk. A lot of plot points and characters that disappear for whole books and don't turn up or come to fruition until 3 books down the line. You have to play the long game, but my God the character development and pay off is worth it. <br/><br/>This feels very much like Ciri's </span>
  <span id="freeText4949287189111411159" style="display:none">I'm currently self isolating with covid 19 symptoms and this was everything I needed right now.<br /><br />As I always say in these Witcher reviews - these books are not going to be for everyone. There's a lot of, often dry, political and court talk. A lot of plot points and characters that disappear for whole books and don't turn up or come to fruition until 3 books down the line. You have to play the long game, but my God the character development and pay off is worth it. <br /><br />This feels very much like Ciri's book - and she's not been having a good time. She feels very alone, abandoned by those she thought would always be there to protect her, and badly hurting. Physically and mentally. As we see her unravel and tell her story of what's happened to her since leaving the coup at Thanedd, we get a wave of mixed emotions and a young woman who's had a lot of growing up to do in a short amount of time. Her character development has been masterfully done over the last couple of books, and we've been left with a deeply complicated character who has faced some horrendous situations and made some very difficult decisions.<br /><br />Because this feels like Ciri's story, we do see less of Geralt and Yennefer - although they are busy in the background continuing the search for lion cub. Their stories aren't as interesting, granted, however I always love the banter between Geralt and his band of misfits, and it was also nice to get a bit more background on Yen. We also (finally) get to visit the Isles of Skellige and return to the character of Crach en Craite, which I found very exciting and atmospheric. The audio certainly helped in this respect as the narrator did an excellent job of a variation on several Scottish accents to set the Skellige scene.<br /><br />I found this to be an excellent addition to the series, finally with some long term plot payoff. The webs are slowly closing in on our protagonists and I feel as though the final ending is going to be epic. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4949287189111411159" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1633303384" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1633303384" />
    <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc"><img alt="Mogsy (MMOGC)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286325553p2/4379514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1633303384?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mogsy (MMOGC)" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc">Mogsy (MMOGC)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316273718" href="/book/show/27917672-the-tower-of-swallows">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1633303384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8563558593309649158">3.5 of 5 stars at the BiblioSanctum <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://bibliosanctum.com/2016/05/24/audiobook-review-the-tower-of-swallows-by-andrzej-sapkowski/'>https://bibliosanctum.com/2016/05/24/...</a><br/><br/>I am so in love with these audiobooks. Peter Kenny is the incontrovertible voice of this series, making all my favorite characters come to life with his authentic reading style and superb acting. Fan translations of these books have been around for a while, but I don’t mind waiting longer if it means I can enjoy the audio editions; every time I jump into a new book, it’s like coming home to old friends.<br/><br/>The Tower of Swall</span>
  <span id="freeText8563558593309649158" style="display:none">3.5 of 5 stars at the BiblioSanctum <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://bibliosanctum.com/2016/05/24/audiobook-review-the-tower-of-swallows-by-andrzej-sapkowski/">https://bibliosanctum.com/2016/05/24/...</a><br /><br />I am so in love with these audiobooks. Peter Kenny is the incontrovertible voice of this series, making all my favorite characters come to life with his authentic reading style and superb acting. Fan translations of these books have been around for a while, but I don’t mind waiting longer if it means I can enjoy the audio editions; every time I jump into a new book, it’s like coming home to old friends.<br /><br />The Tower of Swallows picks up from the end of Baptism of Fire, where the search for Ciri continues. The story begins by mirroring the intro of the previous book with a long convalescence of one of our characters, this time Ciri instead of Geralt. The young princess-turned-Witcher has adopted a new identity and settled into life with a party of young rebels who call themselves the Rats. Something happens, however, leading to her being found unconscious and gravely injured in the middle of a swamp by an old hermit named Vysogota. The old man nurses her back to health, and during her recovery Ciri tells him what happened.<br /><br />Meanwhile, Geralt and his companions are still traveling together trying to find Ciri, but their precarious alliance keeps coming under fire from distrust and infighting, not to mention plenty of bad decisions. There’s also a lot of political intrigue happening in the background as their enemies keep plotting against them, and a new face of evil enters the field.<br /><br />While I really enjoyed The Tower of Swallows, I have to confess it wasn’t my favorite. In fact, this was the first full-length Witcher novel in which I felt the pacing stumbled a little. After an incredibly strong beginning, the story loses steam around the halfway point when it takes a very sudden turn in a new direction. We go abruptly from fast-paced action and adventure to convoluted politics, which made the end of the book tedious and hard to understand when compared to the first half.<br /><br />Still, this is a book you won’t want to miss, especially if you’ve been following along with the series, and the good parts made it all worth it. One of the things I admire most about Andrzej Sapkowski’s storytelling is the way he experiments with different narrative styles, which sometimes involve sudden jumps in the timeline and frequent switches in points-of-view. Normally I am not a fan of this; however, I love the interesting and engaging way Sapkowski does it, as illustrated at the beginning of the novel, where the events that befell Ciri are unraveled by having her share her story with Vysogota. Narrative threads are picked up, dropped, picked up again by different characters, but done in a seamless way that flows well and is easy to follow, even in the audio format.<br /><br />The characters are also evolving nicely with each installment. Notably, Ciri has come of age and she is settling in as one of the series’ major characters. She’s still finding her way in this book, both literally and figuratively. Torn between her old life as a princess and her new one as a rogue Witcher, she’s frequently waffling on what she wants, and like many troubled teens she is quick to anger especially when confronted with hard truths. She may be an expert fighter, but at the end of the day she’s still just a lost young girl. Geralt is of course the other central figure, and here he suffers his own crisis of confidence, beating himself up for not doing all he can to find Ciri, at some points even convincing himself that she is dead and that his quest is futile. He also clashes with his companions, in particular with Cahir the Nilfgaardian, whom Geralt does not trust. Overall, lack of success has demoralized the party, causing rising tensions and fraying nerves. It almost makes you want to break out the popcorn and watch the fur fly.<br /><br />Even though the second half is slow, the book does ends with a bang, making me excited for what’s coming next. In total, there are currently six books translated into English and produced in audio, including two that are story collections. I have a feeling all the questions will be answered and everything will come together as the series heads towards its conclusion.<br /><br />Narration-wise, I really have no complaints. Peter Kenny has already won me over, and he’s probably the biggest reason why I’m such a diehard fan of the Witcher audiobooks, to the extent now where no other format will do. I’m just sad knowing that the next book will be the final entry in the saga. Regardless, I’m looking forward to seeing how it’s all going to end.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8563558593309649158" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2020-shelf">2020-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3222775362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11036197436553997209">This is some hardcore cool Fantasy. Far from having any kind of tired storyline, it always feels fresh and surprising even though, by all rights, it OUGHT to fall into so rather obvious directions because... we WANT it. <br/><br/>But that's where the joy comes in. :) The pacing is fast and just when you think you've got a handle on certain things, there's always that little wrench in the works. :)<br/><br/>I admit I teared up during certain events. And it isn't entirely isolated with events featuring only Ciri. She</span>
  <span id="freeText11036197436553997209" style="display:none">This is some hardcore cool Fantasy. Far from having any kind of tired storyline, it always feels fresh and surprising even though, by all rights, it OUGHT to fall into so rather obvious directions because... we WANT it. <br /><br />But that's where the joy comes in. :) The pacing is fast and just when you think you've got a handle on certain things, there's always that little wrench in the works. :)<br /><br />I admit I teared up during certain events. And it isn't entirely isolated with events featuring only Ciri. She's really come into her own, but I'm still a huge fan of Geralt. And to wait THAT long for Yennifer? For shame!<br /><br />Doesn't matter. This is an unusual enough fantasy novel to keep old fans of the genre hopping and new fans constantly interested. I can't imagine where any hater would be coming from. :)</span>

<div id="review_2056964584" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2056964584" />
    <a title="Celise" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4653644-celise"><img alt="Celise" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546382482p2/4653644.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2056964584?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celise" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celise" href="/user/show/4653644-celise">Celise</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/29340636-the-tower-of-swallows">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4653644-celise?shelf=owned-read">owned-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4653644-celise?shelf=fantasy-adult">fantasy-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2056964584" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer304318928557245261">Buddy read with Markus, who actually led me to discover this amazing series in the first place.<br/><br/>The previous book in The Witcher series was a little bit choppy, with each change in point of view requiring some adjustment. By comparison, The Tower of Swallows is like a river being fed by a bunch of little streams. All of the different characters' scenes flow easily together to tell the larger story, and as a reader it's so easy to be carried along the current while observing all of the terrible th</span>
  <span id="freeText304318928557245261" style="display:none">Buddy read with Markus, who actually led me to discover this amazing series in the first place.<br /><br />The previous book in The Witcher series was a little bit choppy, with each change in point of view requiring some adjustment. By comparison, The Tower of Swallows is like a river being fed by a bunch of little streams. All of the different characters' scenes flow easily together to tell the larger story, and as a reader it's so easy to be carried along the current while observing all of the terrible things that happen on the banks. Real life seems far off when you're sucked into something like that, and that's what I look for in a good book!<br /><br />As for the plot, I won't bother to summarize. This is the 6th book in the series, so if you're already reading them you'll get to this one on your own. If you haven't read any of The Witcher series, I recommend reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1128434.The_Last_Wish__The_Witcher___1_" title="The Last Wish (The Witcher, #1) by Andrzej Sapkowski" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Wish</a>, the short story anthology that begins everything. If you're more interested in jumping to the novels, here is my review for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1917549623" rel="nofollow noopener">Blood of Elves</a>.<br /><br />If you're a Ciri fan and felt like she was sorely missed in Baptism of Fire, here's one for you! Her parts were ace. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Her first encounter with Bonhart actually had my heart racing. The fighting pit was also just so cool, and truthfully I wanted a little bit more of that.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Ciri begins this novel in the company of an interesting character named Vysogota, to whom she reveals the story of her recent encounters, and so reveals them to the reader. Vysogota himself, while not focused on too much, still has a big impact and his parts are so poetically written.<br /><br />This installment in particular feels very high fantasy with how much it covered both geographically and story-wise.The imagery is also inspired and vividly described. The forests are wet and covered in colourful mushrooms, the caves are decorated with rose-coloured stalactites. Most of the fantasy I've read tends to get stuck with the good old green, brown and grey palette, but it's nice to change it up sometimes. I think it will be easy to remember the really good scenes from this book due to the fact that they all are described with such different and colourful visuals.<br /><br />I think this one is probably my favourite book in the saga after <i>The Time of Contempt.</i><br /><br />And just a quick note to say I started the next book, <i> Lady of the Lake </i> and at about 5 pages in my mind was already blown.</span>
  <a data-text-id="304318928557245261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2785467354" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11395345712169465642">I continue to be confused by this series. It's like having that moody coworker, and you never know which mood they'll be in when they show up in the morning. Will they be the life of the party, and you'll have the best shift ever? Will they show up grumpy and make you want to leave in ten minutes? <br/><br/>I never know if the next book I open will be full of adventures and delightfully horrifying creatures that Geralt and Ciri beat against all odds OR if we're going to have a dry, pointless installment t</span>
  <span id="freeText11395345712169465642" style="display:none">I continue to be confused by this series. It's like having that moody coworker, and you never know which mood they'll be in when they show up in the morning. Will they be the life of the party, and you'll have the best shift ever? Will they show up grumpy and make you want to leave in ten minutes? <br /><br />I never know if the next book I open will be full of adventures and delightfully horrifying creatures that Geralt and Ciri beat against all odds OR if we're going to have a dry, pointless installment that spends hundreds of pages analyzing a political system. Fortunately, or unfortunately, this book was somewhere in between. <br /><br />The majority of the book followed Ciri with some cut scenes to Geralt. If you're looking for "main story line" material, this is that book. If you're looking for side quests with monsters and lore, this is not that book. <br /><br />I'd rate this book an R for violence, swearing, and sexual references.</span>

<div id="review_2357630151" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9135296463702699705">If a picture is worth a thousand words, the illustration on the cover contains almost as much excitement as the entire 400+ page novel.<br/><br/>I will finish this series because I'm already six books deep, but I will do so begrudgingly. <i>The Witcher</i> stopped being fun about three books ago and instead became a massive (and tedious) fake history lesson.<br/><br/>I don't care about the politics anymore. It's not intriguing. It's not interesting. It's work; it's work remembering everyone's names, it's work keeping trac</span>
  <span id="freeText9135296463702699705" style="display:none">If a picture is worth a thousand words, the illustration on the cover contains almost as much excitement as the entire 400+ page novel.<br /><br />I will finish this series because I'm already six books deep, but I will do so begrudgingly. <i>The Witcher</i> stopped being fun about three books ago and instead became a massive (and tedious) fake history lesson.<br /><br />I don't care about the politics anymore. It's not intriguing. It's not interesting. It's work; it's work remembering everyone's names, it's work keeping track of the timeline as the narration shifts back and forth between dozens of characters, and it's work trying to stay awake and attentive while a protagonist with two swords strapped to his back sits around talking for fifty pages at a time.<br /><br />I wish I had just stuck to the games.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9135296463702699705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3210371384" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3210371384" />
    <a title="Amanda NEVER MANDY" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36873041-amanda-never-mandy"><img alt="Amanda NEVER MANDY" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562165941p2/36873041.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3210371384?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda NEVER MANDY" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda NEVER MANDY" href="/user/show/36873041-amanda-never-mandy">Amanda NEVER MANDY</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316273718" href="/book/show/27917672-the-tower-of-swallows">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36873041-amanda-never-mandy?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36873041-amanda-never-mandy?shelf=the-witcher">the-witcher</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3210371384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14070003795322007987"><b>
  <i>Ciri makes a new friend when her wounded heart needs one the most and Geralt continues on his path to reach her before the wrong people do.</i>
</b><br/><br/>The group of people that are forming around Geralt fascinate me. Each individual person has their own unique story and it is enough to make the reader want to pause the current story to delve into their backstories. I do applaud an author that takes the time to bring that extra to each character and doesn’t just insert them as a generic bit to carry the s</span>
  <span id="freeText14070003795322007987" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Ciri makes a new friend when her wounded heart needs one the most and Geralt continues on his path to reach her before the wrong people do.</i>
</b><br /><br />The group of people that are forming around Geralt fascinate me. Each individual person has their own unique story and it is enough to make the reader want to pause the current story to delve into their backstories. I do applaud an author that takes the time to bring that extra to each character and doesn’t just insert them as a generic bit to carry the story along. There is one member of the group that stands out the most and I would have no problem reading a book or two that focuses on just them and what all they were up to before meeting Geralt. I won’t say more than that here because I hate reviews that spoil even the smallest detail.<br /><br />The beginning of this book had me thinking I was reading the best book in the series. The middle drifted off and got a smidge boring with a lot of talk about the warring factions. The ending did pick back up and was almost enough to wash out the bad taste left by the middle but not quite. I did like the way it was told. It differed from the previous books and that was something interesting to behold. Not always does stepping out and trying something new work for a person so it was awesome to see that it did here.<br /><br />Four stars to the first book in the saga to cause my attention span to drift a little.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14070003795322007987" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2126571122" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2126571122" />
    <a title="Anirudh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16686132-anirudh"><img alt="Anirudh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1359010972p2/16686132.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2126571122?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anirudh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anirudh" href="/user/show/16686132-anirudh">Anirudh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316273718" href="/book/show/27917672-the-tower-of-swallows">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16686132-anirudh?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2126571122" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16832580400282120812">When I began reading the Witcher Saga, as I made progress through the series a fear began to grow in me. Although I dismissed it at first, now I've come to the realisation that it was true. Sapkowski had a story big enough for a novella and stretched it over five books. <br/><br/>The book starts well and one gets the false sense of hope that the book is finally getting somewhere after the disaster of the previous books. But one soon realises that despite turning page after page we get no where because the</span>
  <span id="freeText16832580400282120812" style="display:none">When I began reading the Witcher Saga, as I made progress through the series a fear began to grow in me. Although I dismissed it at first, now I've come to the realisation that it was true. Sapkowski had a story big enough for a novella and stretched it over five books. <br /><br />The book starts well and one gets the false sense of hope that the book is finally getting somewhere after the disaster of the previous books. But one soon realises that despite turning page after page we get no where because there really was nowhere to go to begin with. The witcher, briefly in action slumps back into a moaning child who is anything but a fearsome warrior I had imagined him to be. <br /><br />Ciri on the other hand is a puzzle. I am not sure what her intended destiny is or in which direction she was meant to take, but it this book she is everywhere. No amount of logic helped me figure out how a girl who was happily playing bandit for no apparent reason suddenly insists she's a witcher and decides to take on a difficult task which is not even a task for the witcher. At the end of the story her story line reaches such absurdity that I am afraid there will be no recovery from it. <br /><br />The narration plays out interestingly in this book and PoV is switched between characters as well as storylines. Although this is an interesting take and many times creates an entertaining interplay between characters and situations, at time this can be quite confusing to grasp without several re reads.<br /><br />Overall this is a disappointing read. <b>The extra star is purely out of sentiment, for fond adventures of old and in hope for new adventures that will never come to be.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16832580400282120812" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3188952031" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3188952031" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3188952031?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda Hupe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda Hupe" href="/user/show/11658047-amanda-hupe">Amanda Hupe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316273718" href="/book/show/27917672-the-tower-of-swallows">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11658047-amanda-hupe?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3188952031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16651123560048824760">I decided to wait to read The Tower of Swallows by Andrzej Sapkowski because I was going through the series too fast. I wanted to be able to enjoy it a bit more. This is the 4th book in the series, which means I am almost done. Once again, Geralt joined with Milva, Regis, Cahir, and Dandelion, who are still in search of Ciri. They know about the fake Ciri who is intended to marry the Nilfgaard emperor. However, there is no other evidence that the real Ciri is alive. She was last with a group of </span>
  <span id="freeText16651123560048824760" style="display:none">I decided to wait to read The Tower of Swallows by Andrzej Sapkowski because I was going through the series too fast. I wanted to be able to enjoy it a bit more. This is the 4th book in the series, which means I am almost done. Once again, Geralt joined with Milva, Regis, Cahir, and Dandelion, who are still in search of Ciri. They know about the fake Ciri who is intended to marry the Nilfgaard emperor. However, there is no other evidence that the real Ciri is alive. She was last with a group of bandits who made a name for themselves. Even still, her enemies are gathering. The only place that may help is the tower of swallows.<br /><br />This installment picks up right where book 3 left. That is the bittersweet aspect of the books, yes, they end abruptly, but the beginning always dives right into the story. I absolutely fell in love with this series since the very first book. While I loved this book. This one does jump around more than the previous books. In the beginning, this creates a relatively slow pace but the tension really builds up throughout with a pretty epic conclusion. (Don’t worry, I won’t give spoilers.)<br /><br />I hated Mistle and the Rats group. Yes, they took care of Ciri in a way, but they also took advantage of her. However, I do love that Ciri does get a taste of freedom. She has seen and experienced so much hardship and heartache. Her character development is phenomenal and it is the main focus of this book.<br /><br />Geralt, Milva, Cahir, Regis, and Dandelion are still together and I want them all to be my best friends. They are not close to perfect but they all compliment each other. They are a team and I know this will probably end badly but I am totally okay with them always being together fighting injustice. I really can’t wait until the show catches up with this part of the story.<br /><br />I rate this book 4 out of 5 stars! I will hopefully get to read the next book, Lady of the Lake next month.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16651123560048824760" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
