<div id="review_3230279039" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3230279039" />
    <a title="Doug" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33038913-doug"><img alt="Doug" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515035780p2/33038913.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3230279039?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Doug" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Doug" href="/user/show/33038913-doug">Doug</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/29340636-the-tower-of-swallows">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3230279039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14673278463443886587">I like the continuation of the story, but there are some really bizarre creative, story-telling decisions being made here.<br/><br/>The first is that this whole book is told from the point of view of flashbacks nested within flashbacks. There are multiple flashbacks for various characters, nested within each other. And to make matters worse, you might finish a chapter, dedicated to a certain group of characters, and then move onto the next chapter, but find that it is about a different collection of neste</span>
  <span id="freeText14673278463443886587" style="display:none">I like the continuation of the story, but there are some really bizarre creative, story-telling decisions being made here.<br /><br />The first is that this whole book is told from the point of view of flashbacks nested within flashbacks. There are multiple flashbacks for various characters, nested within each other. And to make matters worse, you might finish a chapter, dedicated to a certain group of characters, and then move onto the next chapter, but find that it is about a different collection of nested flashbacks, but not even finish the flashbacks from the previous chapter before it moves on. So, you will revisit that set of nested flashbacks in maybe 100 pages when it returns to that set.<br /><br />I actually find it interesting and exciting when authors in genre fiction test out different storytelling styles. So, I wouldn't have minded this in principle. The major problem was that the whole book (from the first page) is like this, and it feels like the flashbacks should have wrapped up and caught up to the present by about halfway through the book. Not last for the entire book.<br /><br />That being said, I really do like seeing the characters sprint towards the series finale in the next book. Definitely, storytelling oddities have been on my mind since I finished the short-story collections, but the plot and characters here have really been well-done.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14673278463443886587" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1590962156" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3872927793873581447">It pains my heart to announce it but this one was my least favourite of all. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464111761ra/19198587.gif' width='350' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>I had hard time connecting with characters. Ciri seemed somehow brusque and annoying, Yennefer did hell know what (her charm and wit lost to the unknown), Geralt was lost to the plot and his own doubts, the amazing party traveling that was amazingly executed in #3 was scattered like exploded paint can. The dialogues are somehow stagnant and seem unrealistic, most of the book felt more like "talking", not actually getti</span>
  <span id="freeText3872927793873581447" style="display:none">It pains my heart to announce it but this one was my least favourite of all. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464111761ra/19198587.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I had hard time connecting with characters. Ciri seemed somehow brusque and annoying, Yennefer did hell know what (her charm and wit lost to the unknown), Geralt was lost to the plot and his own doubts, the amazing party traveling that was amazingly executed in #3 was scattered like exploded paint can. The dialogues are somehow stagnant and seem unrealistic, most of the book felt more like "talking", not actually getting things done. It just felt like the painful "filler" book you had to endure before the finale one. <br><br>But I still love papa Sapkowski. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1701930960" />
    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1701930960?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mizuki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mizuki" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki">Mizuki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789863191940" href="/book/show/28941215">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=fairies-related">fairies-related</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=chinese-translation">chinese-translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=pretty-good">pretty-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=supernatural-stuff">supernatural-stuff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1701930960" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15864099655167116446">The more I read into this series, the more I have doubts with it. For example, why the people in this high fantasy 'swords & magic' world are using terms which are very similar with us modern men and women's? Why they seem to know about genetic engineering? Does this mean the humans in this world had once come from <i>our world</i>, somehow?<br/><br/>Still, aside from my doubts and the lack of explanation, I still found myself enjoying this series. The characters are still going strong whilst the political schem</span>
  <span id="freeText15864099655167116446" style="display:none">The more I read into this series, the more I have doubts with it. For example, why the people in this high fantasy 'swords &amp; magic' world are using terms which are very similar with us modern men and women's? Why they seem to know about genetic engineering? Does this mean the humans in this world had once come from <i>our world</i>, somehow?<br /><br />Still, aside from my doubts and the lack of explanation, I still found myself enjoying this series. The characters are still going strong whilst the political schemes plots are getting quite tiresome (too many schemes within too many different courts, I lost count). And OMG! I like the development with Ciri this time, she suffered so much and eventually, she pushed through! I wonder what will happen in the next book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15864099655167116446" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7Gn/zXfuRPwXXlxLsv+S6zpE1K6k1kIN3OniJHxQytNSNdci4DEWi2Q7tKnZkfN/fv8YjQId1WVnL0mgTYa7hQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tjQ/zjTa3xZy0rOb/uk6u+2/3pXjeIVngbnC5Y0yLBAIaBchowWNYQG3W3mVh1svqQQStkWzEg86f2lhvORdRg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/38569.Andrzej_Sapkowski">About Andrzej Sapkowski</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/38569.Andrzej_Sapkowski"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1241014902p3/38569.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/38569.Andrzej_Sapkowski">Andrzej Sapkowski
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
11,109
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13717141512782443515">Andrzej Sapkowski, born June 21, 1948 in Łódź, is a Polish fantasy writer. Sapkowski studied economics, and before turning to writing, he had worked as a senior sales representative for a foreign trade company. His first short story, The Witcher (Wiedźmin), was published in Fantastyka, Poland's leading fantasy literary magazine, in 1986 and was enormously successful both with readers and critics. </span>
  <span id="freeText13717141512782443515" style="display:none">Andrzej Sapkowski, born June 21, 1948 in Łódź, is a Polish fantasy writer. Sapkowski studied economics, and before turning to writing, he had worked as a senior sales representative for a foreign trade company. His first short story, The Witcher (Wiedźmin), was published in Fantastyka, Poland's leading fantasy literary magazine, in 1986 and was enormously successful both with readers and critics. Sapkowski has created a cycle of tales based on the world of The Witcher, comprising three collections of short stories and five novels. This cycle and his many other works have made him one of the best-known fantasy authors in Poland in the 1990s.<br /><br />The main character of The Witcher (alternative translation: The Hexer) is Geralt, a mutant assassin who has been trained since childhood to hunt down and destroy monsters. Geralt exists in an ambiguous moral universe, yet manages to maintain his own coherent code of ethics. At the same time cynical and noble, Geralt has been compared to Raymond Chandler's signature character Philip Marlowe. The world in which these adventures take place is heavily influenced by Slavic mythology.<br /><br />Sapkowski has won five Zajdel Awards, including three for short stories "Mniejsze zło" (Lesser Evil) (1990), "Miecz przeznaczenia" (Sword of Destiny) (1992) and "W leju po bombie" (In a Bomb Crater) (1993), and two for the novels "Krew elfów" (Blood of Elves) (1994) and "Narrenturm" (2002). He also won the Spanish Ignotus Award, best anthology, for The Last Wish in 2003, and for "Muzykanci" (The Musicians), best foreign short story, same year.<br /><br />In 1997, Sapkowski won the prestigious Polityka's Passport award, which is awarded annually to artists who have strong prospects for international success.<br /><br />In 2001, a Television Series based on the Witcher cycle was released in Poland and internationally, entitled Wiedźmin (The Hexer). A film by the same title was compiled from excerpts of the television series but both have been critical and box office failures.<br /><br />Sapkowski's books have been translated into Czech, Russian, Lithuanian, German, Spanish, French, Ukrainian, and Portuguese. An English translation of The Last Wish short story collection was published by Gollancz in 2007.<br /><br />The Polish game publisher, CD Projekt, created a role-playing PC game based on this universe, called The Witcher, which was released in October 2007. There is also a mobile version of the game which has been created by Breakpoint Games and is being published by Hands-On Mobile in Western Europe,Latin America and Asia Pacific.<br /><br />The English translation of Sapkowski's novel Blood of Elves won the David Gemmell Legends Award in 2009.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13717141512782443515" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/trivia/work/66349-wie-a-jask-ki">Trivia About Wieża Jaskółki (S...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
        <div class="mediumText">No trivia or quizzes yet. <a href="/trivia/work/66349-wie-a-jask-ki">Add some now &raquo;</a></div>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>


      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/66349-wie-a-jask-ki">Quotes from Wieża Jaskółki</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Lepiej bez celu iść naprzód niż bez celu stać w miejscu, a z pewnością o niebo lepiej, niż bez celu się cofać.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/186222-lepiej-bez-celu-i-naprz-d-ni-bez-celu-sta-w">41 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Why should I give up revenge? On behalf of what? Moral principles? And what of the higher order of things, in which evil deeds are punished? For you, a philosopher and ethicist, an act of revenge is bad, disgraceful, unethical and illegal. But I ask: where is the punishment for evil? Who has it and grants access? The Gods, in which you do not believe? The great demiurge-creator, which you decided to replace the gods with? Or maybe the law? [...] I know what evil is afraid of. Not your ethics, Vysogota, not your preaching or moral treaties on the life of dignity. Evil is afraid of pain, mutilation, suffering and at the end of the day, death! The dog howls when it is badly wounded! Writhing on the ground and growls, watching the blood flow from its veins and arteries, seeing the bone that sticks out from a stump, watching its guts escape its open belly, feeling the cold as death is about to take them. Then and only then will evil begin to beg, 'Have mercy! I regret my sins! I'll be good, I swear! Just save me, do not let me waste away!'. Yes, hermit. That is the way to fight evil! When evil wants to harm you, inflict pain - anticipate them, it's best if evil does not expect it. But if you fail to prevent evil, if you have been hurt by evil, then avenge him! It is best when they have already forgotten, when they feel safe. Then pay them in double. In triple. An eye for an eye? No! Both eyes for an eye! A tooth for a tooth? No! All their teeth for a tooth! Repay evil! Make it wail in pain, howling until their eyes pop from their sockets. And then, you can look under your feet and boldly declare that what is there cannot endanger anyone, cannot hurt anyone. How can someone be a danger, when they have no eyes? How can someone hurt when they have no hands? They can only wait until they bleed to death.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/7307803-why-should-i-give-up-revenge-on-behalf-of-what">36 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a class="actionLink" style="float: right" href="/work/quotes/66349-wie-a-jask-ki">More quotes&hellip;</a>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
